 2008. We were formed to engage in the business of marketing
 developing
 and producing unique
 proprietary water products.&nbsp;&nbsp;Our original intended line of enhanced bottled waters was based upon the experience and expertise of our founder
 designed to make everyday hydration and nutrition a more enjoyable experience.&nbsp;&nbsp;In May of 2008
 we commenced our development stage operations
 and had no significant assets. In May 2010
 we abandoned our pursuit of the proprietary bottled water business.


 2008
 through December 31
 2012
 we have not generated any revenues and have incurred net losses of $704
773. In May of 2008
 our only business activity was the formation of our corporate entity and the development of our business model.&nbsp;&nbsp;On July 11
 2008
 we filed an S-1 Registration Statement with the Securities and Exchange Commission (the &#147;SEC&#148;)
 and the registration statement became effective on July 18
 2008.


 2008
 we closed our direct public offering and were able to raise $55
000 as proposed.&nbsp;&nbsp;The proceeds of the offering enabled us to maintain our operations and working capital requirements for approximately 12 months. During that time
 we investigated various financing options and opportunities. No additional business operations have occurred nor has any revenue been generated as of the year ended December 31
 2012.

 reorganizations and mergers with businesses or entities that desire to avoid what such entities may deem to be the adverse factors related to an initial public offering (&#147;IPO&#148;) as a method of going public. The most prevalent of these factors include substantial time requirements
 legal and accounting costs
 the inability to obtain an underwriter who is willing to publicly offer and sell shares
 the lack of or the inability to obtain the required financial statements for such an undertaking
 state limitations on the amount of dilution to public investors in comparison to the shareholders of any such entities
 along with other conditions or requirements imposed by various federal and state securities laws
 rules and regulations and federal and state agencies that implement such laws
 rules and regulations.







 along with required audited
 interim and proforma financial statements
 within four business days of the closing of any such transaction (Item 5.01(a)(8) of Form 8-K); and the recent amendments to Rule 144 adopted by the SEC that were effective on February 15
 2008
 limit the resale of most securities of shell companies until one year after the filing of such information
 may eliminate many of the perceived advantages of these types of going public transactions.&nbsp;&nbsp;These types of transactions are customarily referred to as &#147;reverse&#148; mergers in which the acquired company&#146;s shareholders become controlling shareholders in the acquiring company and the acquiring company becomes the successor to the business operations of the acquired company.&nbsp;&nbsp;Regulations governing shell companies also deny the use of Form S-8 for the registration of securities and limit the use of this Form to a reorganized shell company until the expiration of 60 days from when any such entity is no longer considered to be a shell company.&nbsp;&nbsp;This prohibition could further restrict opportunities for us to acquire companies that may already have stock option plans in place that cover numerous employees.&nbsp;&nbsp;In such instances
 there may be no exemption from registration for the issuance of securities in any business combination to these employees
 thereby necessitating the filing of a registration statement with the SEC to complete any such reorganization
 and incurring the time and expense that are normally avoided by reverse mergers.


 adopted by the SEC and effective on February 15
 2008
 codify the SEC&#146;s prior position limiting the tradeability of certain securities of shell companies
 including those issued by us in any acquisition
 reorganization or merger
 and further limit the tradeability of additional securities of shell companies; these amendments further restrict the availability of opportunities for us to acquire any business or enterprise that desires to utilize us as a means of going public.

&#148; which requires accounting for deferred income taxes under the asset and liability method. &nbsp;Deferred income tax asset and liabilities are computed for difference between the financial statement and tax bases of assets and liabilities that will result in taxable or deductible amounts in the future based on the enacted tax laws and rates applicable to the periods in which the differences are expected to affect taxable income. &nbsp;Valuation allowances are established
 when necessary
 to reduce the deferred income tax assets to the amount expected to be realized.


 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws. &nbsp;Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions. &nbsp;The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities. &nbsp;When facts and circumstances change
 the Company reassesses these probabilities and records any changes in the consolidated financial statements as appropriate.


 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
 based on the technical merits of the position. &nbsp;The tax benefit to be recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that is greater than fifty percent likely of being realized upon ultimate settlement. &nbsp;De-recognition of a tax benefit previously recognized could result in the Company recording a tax liability that would reduce stockholders&#146; equity.

 as Corporate Vice President and Director of Corporate Security and Services at Archer Daniels Midland

 has been

 one of the leading private strategic security advisory and management companies in the U.S. &nbsp;&nbsp;Prior to that

500 sworn officers who comprise the nation's second largest police department and earned a national reputation as a results driven police chief. Prior to that

 he took steps to reduce the burden on crime victims by creating a policy in which the same detective was always assigned to investigate repeat reports from the same victim. He also opened new lines of communication with the public as part of the Chicago Alternative Policing Strategy (CAPS) program. &nbsp;Mr. Hillard served 13 months in Vietnam and received four medals and a Presidential Unit Citation. He entered the Chicago Police Training Academy in 1968 and served as a police officer in several districts and as a specialist in the Gang Crimes Unit. In 1975
 he was shot twice and seriously wounded while apprehending a suspect who had shot four suburban police officers. He subsequently received the Chicago Police Medal
 an Award of Valor. Mr. Hillard holds a Bachelor and Master degrees in Corrections from Chicago State University. In addition
 he has completed training through the Police Executive Research Forum (PERF)
 the FBI National Academy
 the FBI National Executive Institute

 as well as their related disclosures.&amp;nbsp; Such estimates and assumptions also affect the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period.&amp;nbsp; Actual results could differ from those estimates.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;Cash and Cash Equivalents&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;The Company considers short-term interest bearing investments with initial maturities of three months or less to be cash equivalents. Cash and cash equivalents consist of cash in banks
 free credit on investment accounts and money market accounts.&amp;nbsp; &lt;/font&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;The Company &lt;/font&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;ha&lt;/font&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;s&lt;/font&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt; no cash or cash equivalents.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:0pt&quot; lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;Income Taxes&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot; lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;The Company&amp;#146;s taxable income or loss is included in the consolidated income tax returns of the Company&amp;#146;s parent. Current and deferred income taxes are allocated to the members of the consolidated group as if each member were a separate taxpayer. &lt;/font&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;The Company accounts for income taxes in accordance with FASB ASC Topic 740 &amp;#147;Income Taxes
&amp;#148; which requires accounting for deferred income taxes under the asset and liability method.&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp; Deferred income tax asset and liabilities are computed for difference between the financial statement and tax bases of assets and liabilities that will result in taxable or deductible amounts in the future based on the enacted tax laws and rates applicable to the periods in which the differences are expected to affect taxable income.&amp;nbsp; Valuation allowances are established
 when necessary
 to reduce the deferred income tax assets to the amount expected to be realized.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot; lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;The determination of the Company&amp;#146;s provision for income taxes requires significant judgment
 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws.&amp;nbsp; Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions.&amp;nbsp; The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&amp;#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities.&amp;nbsp; When facts and circumstances change
 the Company reassesses these probabilities and records any changes in the consolidated financial statements as appropriate.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot; lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;In accordance with GAAP
 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
 based on the technical merits of the position.&amp;nbsp; The tax benefit to be recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that is greater than fifty percent likely of being realized upon ultimate settlement.&amp;nbsp; De-recognition of a tax benefit previously recognized could result in the Company recording a tax liability that would reduce stockholders&amp;#146; equity.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;br clear=&quot;all&quot; style=&quot;PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always&quot;&gt;&lt;/br&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;This policy also provides guidance on thresholds
 measurement
 de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition that is intended to provide better consolidated financial statement comparability among different entities.&amp;nbsp; Management&amp;#146;s conclusions regarding this policy may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including
 but not limited to
 on-going analyses of and changes to tax laws
 regulations and interpretations thereof.&amp;nbsp; Generally
 the tax filings are no longer subject to income tax examinations by major taxing authorities for years before 2008. Any potential examinations may include questioning the timing and amount of deductions
 the nexus of income among various tax jurisdictions and compliance with U.S. federal
 state and local tax laws.&amp;nbsp; The Company&apos;s management does not expect that the total amount of unrecognized tax benefits will materially change over the next twelve months. &lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot; lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;Interest and Penalty Recognition on Unrecognized Tax Benefits&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot; lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot; lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;The Company recognizes interest accrued related to unrecognized tax benefits in interest expense and penalties in other operational expenses. No interest expense or penalties have been recognized as of and for the years ended December 31
 2012 and 2011.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;Fair Value of Financial Instruments&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt; &lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;The fair values of the Company&amp;#146;s assets and liabilities that qualify as financial instruments under FASB ASC Topic 825

 &amp;#147;Earnings Per Share.&amp;#148; Basic loss per common share is computed by dividing net loss available to common stockholders by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during the period.&amp;nbsp; Diluted loss per common share incorporates the dilutive effect of common stock equivalents on an average basis during the period.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;The calculation of diluted net loss per share excludes 1

 since their effect is anti-dilutive. All per share calculations reflect the effects of the reverse stock split. &lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;Loss Contingencies&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;X-NONE&quot;&gt;The Company recognizes contingent losses that are both probable and estimable.&amp;nbsp; In this context
 the Company defines probability as circumstances under which events are likely to occur.&amp;nbsp; In regards to legal cost
 we record such costs as incurred.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;Nonemployee awards&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;The fair value of equity instruments issued to a nonemployee is measured by using the stock price and other measurement assumptions as of the earlier date of either: (i) a commitment for performance by the nonemployee has been reached; or (ii) the counterparty&amp;#146;s performance is complete.&amp;nbsp; Expenses related to nonemployee awards are generally recognized in the same period as the Company incurs the related liability for goods and services received.&amp;nbsp; &lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;Recently Adopted Accounting Pronouncements &lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;In October 2012
 the FASB issued Accounting Standards Update (&amp;#147;ASU&amp;#148;) 2012-04
 &amp;#147;&lt;i&gt;Technical Corrections and Improvements&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#148; in Accounting Standards Update No. 2012-04. The amendments in this update cover a wide range of Topics in the Accounting Standards Codification. These amendments include technical corrections and improvements to the Accounting Standards Codification and conforming amendments related to fair value measurements. The amendments in this update will be effective for fiscal periods beginning after December 15
 2012. The adoption of ASU 2012-04 is not expected to have a material impact on the Company&amp;#146;s financial position or results of operations.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;br clear=&quot;all&quot; style=&quot;PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always&quot;&gt;&lt;/br&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt; TEXT-AUTOSPACE:&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;In August 2012

 &lt;i&gt;Intangibles &amp;#150; Goodwill and Other (Topic 350): Testing Indefinite-Lived Intangible Assets for Impairment&lt;/i&gt; and permits an entity first to assess qualitative factors to determine whether it is more likely than not that an indefinite-lived intangible asset is impaired as a basis for determining whether it is necessary to perform the quantitative impairment test in accordance with Subtopic 350-30

These factors raise substantial doubt about the Company&amp;#146;s ability to continue as a going concern. &lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt; TEXT-AUTOSPACE:&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN&quot;&gt;The accompanying financial statements have been prepared assuming that the Company will continue as a going concern
 which contemplates the recoverability of assets and the satisfaction of liabilities in the normal course of business.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;Currently
 the Company has a no cash balance available for the payment of ongoing operating expenses
 and it is dependent on capital contributions and advances from its parent company and its shareholders in order to cover its operational costs to allow it to continue as a going concern.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;Management plans to fund continued operations of the Company by eventually generating profits from operations and raising sufficient capital through placement of its common stock or issuance of debt securities.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt; TEXT-AUTOSPACE:&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN&quot;&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt; TEXT-AUTOSPACE:&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN&quot;&gt;In the event &lt;/font&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;the Company&lt;/font&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN&quot;&gt; does not generate sufficient funds from revenues or financing through the issuance of its common stock or from debt financing

&amp;#148; which requires accounting for deferred income taxes under the asset and liability method.&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp; Deferred income tax asset and liabilities are computed for difference between the financial statement and tax bases of assets and liabilities that will result in taxable or deductible amounts in the future based on the enacted tax laws and rates applicable to the periods in which the differences are expected to affect taxable income.&amp;nbsp; Valuation allowances are established
 when necessary
 to reduce the deferred income tax assets to the amount expected to be realized.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot; lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;The determination of the Company&amp;#146;s provision for income taxes requires significant judgment
 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws.&amp;nbsp; Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions.&amp;nbsp; The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&amp;#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities.&amp;nbsp; When facts and circumstances change
 the Company reassesses these probabilities and records any changes in the consolidated financial statements as appropriate.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;font style=&quot;LETTER-SPACING:-0.1pt&quot; lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;In accordance with GAAP
 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
 based on the technical merits of the position.&amp;nbsp; The tax benefit to be recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that is greater than fifty percent likely of being realized upon ultimate settlement.&amp;nbsp; De-recognition of a tax benefit previously recognized could result in the Company recording a tax liability that would reduce stockholders&amp;#146; equity.&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&lt;br clear=&quot;all&quot; style=&quot;PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:always&quot;&gt;&lt;/br&gt;&lt;/font&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:center; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt; TEXT-AUTOSPACE:&quot; align=&quot;center&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/font&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&quot;TEXT-ALIGN:justify; MARGIN:0cm 0cm 0pt&quot;&gt;&lt;font lang=&quot;EN-US&quot;&gt;This policy also provides guidance on thresholds
 measurement
 de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition that is intended to provide better consolidated financial statement comparability among different entities.&amp;nbsp; Management&amp;#146;s conclusions regarding this policy may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including
 but not limited to
 on-going analyses of and changes to tax laws
 regulations and interpretations thereof.&amp;nbsp; Generally
 the tax filings are no longer subject to income tax examinations by major taxing authorities for years before 2008. Any potential examinations may include questioning the timing and amount of deductions
 the nexus of income among various tax jurisdictions and compliance with U.S. federal

The preparation of financial statements in conformity with GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect certain reported amounts of assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements
The Company considers short-term interest bearing investments with initial maturities of three months or less to be cash equivalents. Cash and cash equivalents consist of cash in banks
The Company accounts for income taxes in accordance with FASB ASC Topic 740 &#147;Income Taxes

 when necessary
The determination of the Company&#146;s provision for income taxes requires significant judgment
 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws.&nbsp; Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions.&nbsp; The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities.&nbsp; When facts and circumstances change
In accordance with GAAP
 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
This policy also provides guidance on thresholds
 measurement
 de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition that is intended to provide better consolidated financial statement comparability among different entities.&nbsp; Management&#146;s conclusions regarding this policy may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including
 but not limited to
 on-going analyses of and changes to tax laws
 regulations and interpretations thereof.&nbsp; Generally
 the tax filings are no longer subject to income tax examinations by major taxing authorities for years before 2008. Any potential examinations may include questioning the timing and amount of deductions
 the nexus of income among various tax jurisdictions and compliance with U.S. federal
The Company recognizes interest accrued related to unrecognized tax benefits in interest expense and penalties in other operational expenses. No interest expense or penalties have been recognized as of and for the years ended December 31

 &#147;Financial Instruments
&#148; approximate their carrying amounts presented in the accompanying financial statements at December 31

 excluding items classified as marketable securities
 include short-term
 highly liquid investments that are both readily convertible to known amounts of cash
 and so near their maturity that they present minimal risk of changes in value because of changes in interest rates. Generally
 only investments with original maturities of three months or less qualify under that definition. Original maturity means original maturity to the entity holding the investment. For example
 both a three-month US Treasury bill and a three-year Treasury note purchased three months from maturity qualify as cash equivalents. However
 a Treasury note purchased three years ago does not become a cash equivalent when its remaining maturity is three months. Compensating balance arrangements that do not legally restrict the withdrawal or usage of cash amounts may be reported as Cash and Cash Equivalents
 while legally restricted deposits held as compensating balances against borrowing arrangements
 contracts entered into with others
 or company statements of intention with regard to particular deposits are not generally reported as cash and cash equivalents.  excluding items classified as marketable securities
 include short-term
 highly liquid investments that are both readily convertible to known amounts of cash
 and so near their maturity that they present minimal risk of changes in value because of changes in interest rates. Generally
 only investments with original maturities of three months or less qualify under that definition. Original maturity means original maturity to the entity holding the investment. For example
 both a three-month US Treasury bill and a three-year Treasury note purchased three months from maturity qualify as cash equivalents. However
 a Treasury note purchased three years ago does not become a cash equivalent when its remaining maturity is three months. Compensating balance arrangements that do not legally restrict the withdrawal or usage of cash amounts may be reported as Cash and Cash Equivalents
 while legally restricted deposits held as compensating balances against borrowing arrangements
 contracts entered into with others
 or company statements of intention with regard to particular deposits are not generally reported as cash and cash equivalents. Includes cash and cash equivalents associated with the entity's continuing operations. Excludes cash and cash equivalents associated with the disposal group (and discontinued operation).

var moreDialog = null;
var Show = {
    Default:'raw'
    more:function( obj ){
        var bClosed = false;
        if( moreDialog != null )
        {
			try
			{
				bClosed = moreDialog.closed;
			}
			catch(e)
			{
				//Per article at http://support.microsoft.com/kb/244375 there is a problem with the WebBrowser control
				// that somtimes causes it to throw when checking the closed property on a child window that has been
				//closed.  So if the exception occurs we assume the window is closed and move on from there.
				bClosed = true;
			}
			if( !bClosed ){
				moreDialog.close();
			}
        }
        obj = obj.parentNode.getElementsByTagName( 'pre' )[0];
		var hasHtmlTag = false;
		var objHtml = '';
		var raw = '';
		//Check for raw HTML
		var nodes = obj.getElementsByTagName( '*' );
		if( nodes.length ){
			objHtml = obj.innerHTML;
		}else{
			if( obj.innerText ){
				raw = obj.innerText;
			}else{
				raw = obj.textContent;
			}

			if( matches && matches.length ){
				objHtml = raw;
				//If there is an html node it will be 1st or 2nd
				//   but we can check a little further.
				var n = Math.min( 5

						hasHtmlTag = true;
						break;
					}
				}
			}
		}
        if( objHtml.length ){
			var html = '';
			if( hasHtmlTag ){
				html = objHtml;
			}else{


'+

					\n+'    body {'+
					\n+'    }'+
					\n+'    table {'+
					\n+'    }'+

More
width=700,height=650,status=0,resizable=yes,menubar=no,toolbar=no,scrollbars=yes);
			moreDialog.document.write( html );
			moreDialog.document.close();
			if( !hasHtmlTag ){
				moreDialog.document.body.style.margin = '0.5em';
			}
        }
        else
        {
			//default view logic

    toggle:function( win
 domLink ){
        var domId = this.Default;
        var doc = win.document;
        var domEl = doc.getElementById( domId );
        domEl.style.display = 'block';
        this.Default = domId == 'raw' ? 'formatted' : 'raw';
        if( domLink ){
            domLink.innerHTML = this.Default == 'raw' ? 'with Text Wrapped' : 'as Filed';
        }
        var domElOpposite = doc.getElementById( this.Default );
        domElOpposite.style.display = 'none';
    }
	LastAR : null
	showAR : function ( link
 id
 win ){
		if( Show.LastAR ){
			Show.hideAR();
		}
		var ref = link;
		do {
			ref = ref.nextSibling;
		} while (ref && ref.nodeName != 'TABLE');
		if (!ref || ref.nodeName != 'TABLE') {
			var tmp = win ?
				win.document.getElementById(id) :
				document.getElementById(id);
			if( tmp ){
				ref = tmp.cloneNode(true);
				ref.id = '';
				link.parentNode.appendChild(ref);
			}
		}
		if( ref ){
			ref.style.display = 'block';
			Show.LastAR = ref;
		}
	}
	toggleNext : function( link ){
		var ref = link;
		do{
			ref = ref.nextSibling;
		}while( ref.nodeName != 'DIV' );
		if( ref.style &&
			ref.style.display &&
			ref.style.display == 'none' ){
			ref.style.display = 'block';
			if( link.textContent ){
				link.textContent = link.textContent.replace( '+'
 '-' );
			}else{
				link.innerText = link.innerText.replace( '+'
 '-' );
			}
		}else{
			ref.style.display = 'none';
			if( link.textContent ){
				link.textContent = link.textContent.replace( '-'
 '+' );
			}else{
				link.innerText = link.innerText.replace( '-'
 '+' );
			}
		}
	}
	hideAR : function(){
		Show.LastAR.style.display = 'none';
	}
}











    
  
      

          

        

      






        
        


        
Northsight Capital Inc. (&#147;Northsight&#148; or &#147;the Company&#148;) is a development stage company incorporated in the State of Nevada on May 21
 2008. The Company was originally formed to engage in the business of marketing
 developing
 and producing unique
 proprietary water products.&nbsp;&nbsp;Northsight&#146;s original intended line of enhanced bottled waters was based upon the experience and expertise of its founder
 designed to make everyday hydration and nutrition a more enjoyable experience.&nbsp;&nbsp;In May of 2008
 the Company commenced its development stage operations
 and had no significant assets.&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company abandoned the proprietary bottled water business in 2010.&nbsp; In May
 2011
 Safe Communications
 Inc. (n/k/a Kuboo
 Inc.) acquired 80% of the Company&#146;s issued and outstanding common stock
 and
 as a result became its parent company. See Note 5
 Change of Control Transactions. The Company is currently considering new business opportunities for its planned operations.

The preparation of financial statements in conformity with GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect certain reported amounts of assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements
 as well as their related disclosures.&nbsp; Such estimates and assumptions also affect the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting period.&nbsp; Actual results could differ from those estimates.


        
The Company considers short-term interest bearing investments with initial maturities of three months or less to be cash equivalents. Cash and cash equivalents consist of cash in banks
 free credit on investment accounts and money market accounts.&nbsp; 


        
The Company accounts for income taxes in accordance with FASB ASC Topic 740 &#147;Income Taxes

 when necessary
The determination of the Company&#146;s provision for income taxes requires significant judgment
 the use of estimates
 and the interpretation and application of complex tax laws.&nbsp; Significant judgment is required in assessing the timing and amounts of deductible and taxable items and the probability of sustaining uncertain tax positions.&nbsp; The benefits of uncertain tax positions are recorded in the Company&#146;s financial statements only after determining a more-likely-than-not probability that the uncertain tax positions will withstand challenge
 if any
 from tax authorities.&nbsp; When facts and circumstances change
In accordance with GAAP
 the Company is required to determine whether a tax position of the Company is more likely than not to be sustained upon examination by the applicable taxing authority
 including resolution of any related appeals or litigation processes
This policy also provides guidance on thresholds
 measurement
 de-recognition
 classification
 interest and penalties
 accounting in interim periods
 disclosure
 and transition that is intended to provide better consolidated financial statement comparability among different entities.&nbsp; Management&#146;s conclusions regarding this policy may be subject to review and adjustment at a later date based on factors including
 but not limited to
 on-going analyses of and changes to tax laws
 regulations and interpretations thereof.&nbsp; Generally
 the tax filings are no longer subject to income tax examinations by major taxing authorities for years before 2008. Any potential examinations may include questioning the timing and amount of deductions
 the nexus of income among various tax jurisdictions and compliance with U.S. federal
 state and local tax laws.&nbsp; The Company's management does not expect that the total amount of unrecognized tax benefits will materially change over the next twelve months. 


        
The Company recognizes interest accrued related to unrecognized tax benefits in interest expense and penalties in other operational expenses. No interest expense or penalties have been recognized as of and for the years ended December 31
 2012 and 2011.


        
The fair values of the Company&#146;s assets and liabilities that qualify as financial instruments under FASB ASC Topic 825
 &#147;Financial Instruments
&#148; approximate their carrying amounts presented in the accompanying financial statements at December 31
 2012 and 2011.


        
The Company complies with the accounting and disclosure requirements of FASB ASC 260
The calculation of diluted net loss per share excludes 1
225
000 warrants as of December 31
 201
 since their effect is anti-dilutive. All per share calculations reflect the effects of the reverse stock split. 


        
The Company recognizes contingent losses that are both probable and estimable.&nbsp; In this context
 the Company defines probability as circumstances under which events are likely to occur.&nbsp; In regards to legal cost
 we record such costs as incurred.


        
        


        
In October 2012
 the FASB issued Accounting Standards Update (&#147;ASU&#148;) 2012-04
&#148; in Accounting Standards Update No. 2012-04. The amendments in this update cover a wide range of Topics in the Accounting Standards Codification. These amendments include technical corrections and improvements to the Accounting Standards Codification and conforming amendments related to fair value measurements. The amendments in this update will be effective for fiscal periods beginning after December 15
In August 2012
 the FASB issued ASU 2012-03

 Technical Amendments Pursuant to SEC Release No. 33-9250
In July 2012
 the FASB issued ASU 2012-02
&#148; in Accounting Standards Update No. 2012-02. This update amends ASU 2011-08
 and permits an entity first to assess qualitative factors to determine whether it is more likely than not that an indefinite-lived intangible asset is impaired as a basis for determining whether it is necessary to perform the quantitative impairment test in accordance with Subtopic 350-30
. The amendments are effective for annual and interim impairment tests performed for fiscal years beginning after September 15
 2012. Early adoption is permitted
 including for annual and interim impairment tests performed as of a date before July 27
 2012
 if a public entity&#146;s financial statements for the most recent annual or interim period have not yet been issued or
 for nonpublic entities
 have not yet been made available for issuance. The adoption of ASU 2012-02 is not expected to have a material impact on the Company&#146;s financial position or results of operations.

 (2) whether the entity's cash and cash equivalents are insured or expose the entity to credit risk
 (3) the classification of any negative balance accounts (overdrafts)
 and (4) the carrying basis of cash equivalents (for example
 at cost) and whether the carrying amount of cash equivalents approximates fair value.
